    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_3488104513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488104513" />
    <a title="Grymm Gevierre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110261611-grymm-gevierre"><img alt="Grymm Gevierre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582658997p2/110261611.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488104513?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grymm Gevierre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grymm Gevierre" href="/user/show/110261611-grymm-gevierre">Grymm Gevierre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488104513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14344175495945802303">This is the second book I read by Texas-turned-Floridian JK Franko. I read this on the heels of the first book in the Talion series. I took the time to check out his website shortly after finishing these two books (and before reviewing each book), and learn a bit about this author, and he is showing no signs of stopping anytime soon. <br/><br/>This book is written from a different angle than the first. Same characters, Susie and Roy, but instead of seeking revenge, they are fleeing the fallout of their cr</span>
  <span id="freeText14344175495945802303" style="display:none">This is the second book I read by Texas-turned-Floridian JK Franko. I read this on the heels of the first book in the Talion series. I took the time to check out his website shortly after finishing these two books (and before reviewing each book), and learn a bit about this author, and he is showing no signs of stopping anytime soon. <br /><br />This book is written from a different angle than the first. Same characters, Susie and Roy, but instead of seeking revenge, they are fleeing the fallout of their crime. Coming from law backgrounds, they are meticulous and nothing is done without a plan. As pointed out early in the first novel, Roy is a strategist. This is true for the second book, too, but they aren’t the only revenge-driven people in the world. <br /><br />The first book was great, the characters were developed and likable—even if they had to get their hands dirty. This book really dives into the characters and brings the story to a more personal level with the duo. I will say that Franko is adept in character development and planning, and that shines in his characters. I imagine he pulled some traits from himself and placed them in Roy. I will say that there are a lot of subplots and characters and it can be a bit much sometimes. If you don’t read the first story you’re going to get lost quickly. I think the author could do away with some unnecessary supporting characters, but overall this is a very good sequel to the first book and he manages to keep all the strands of his plot together and intersecting in a very clever way. I think my favorite part of this series is that I can actually see these events happening in our world, even though it’s fiction.<br /><br /> From the very first line of prologue Franko hooks you in…which is a bit different than the first book where you settled in with Susie and Roy after a prologue about Joan. <br /><br />“Before meeting Susie and Roy, I had never met a murderer.” <br /><br />What a powerful introduction to the second book. He continues this throughout the book, broken up into parts then chapters. For example, in Part 3 we see in the first few paragraphs a grabbing and dark intro about a firearm and Billy Applegate. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14344175495945802303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3342898595" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14033434765606905177">I was looking forward to reading this after reading Eye for Eye last year. It is not necessary to read the first book to enjoy this one, but I advise you start there, to enjoy the story properly.<br/><br/>Susie and Roy are back, still coping with the death of their daughter, but now with added stress of being involved in some way in a number of murders. As time moves on they truly believe that they have committed the perfect murder. However as the body count rises so do the secrets that they individually </span>
  <span id="freeText14033434765606905177" style="display:none">I was looking forward to reading this after reading Eye for Eye last year. It is not necessary to read the first book to enjoy this one, but I advise you start there, to enjoy the story properly.<br /><br />Susie and Roy are back, still coping with the death of their daughter, but now with added stress of being involved in some way in a number of murders. As time moves on they truly believe that they have committed the perfect murder. However as the body count rises so do the secrets that they individually keep.<br /><br />This a brilliant sequel that keeps up the tense writing of the first book. Can they really get away with murder or will they bring themselves down?<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5166262013249125224"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://thebookloversboudoir.wordpress.com/2020/05/02/tooth-for-tooth-by-jk_franko/'>https://thebookloversboudoir.wordpres...</a><br/><br/>This is an impressive thriller. Tooth for Tooth is one of those books you struggle to stop once you get started. I’d never heard of the author before so haven’t read the first book. I think there are a few things that didn’t register as significant as they should have because I don’t know the rest of the story. This didn’t really impact my enjoyment though.   <span id="freeText5166262013249125224" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thebookloversboudoir.wordpress.com/2020/05/02/tooth-for-tooth-by-jk_franko/">https://thebookloversboudoir.wordpres...</a><br /><br />This is an impressive thriller. Tooth for Tooth is one of those books you struggle to stop once you get started. I’d never heard of the author before so haven’t read the first book. I think there are a few things that didn’t register as significant as they should have because I don’t know the rest of the story. This didn’t really impact my enjoyment though. The book is fast-paced, gripping and employs multiple narrators to tell a complex story. Kirsty is my favourite character. I will read the first book because I really want to know her story. This ticked all the boxes for a great thriller: intense action, fast paced, great characters and a twisted plot. I was very impressed. I look forward to reading the first book and reading book three. Well worth a read.</span>

<div id="review_3446106572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3446106572" />
    <a title="Kathleen Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2714432-kathleen-kelly"><img alt="Kathleen Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308841827p2/2714432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3446106572?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen Kelly" href="/user/show/2714432-kathleen-kelly">Kathleen Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3446106572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11081240209245427960">"An eye for an eye, a tooth for a tooth" Revenge is not always best served cold as the saying goes. A Tooth for a Tooth by JK Franko is the second in the Talion Series. Featuring Susie and Roy who have both lost a loved one and go out to commit the perfect murder. Or was it. They find that they become would-be victims in this novel that is very complex in it's writing. Lots of different characters tell the stories of loss and what could be Roy and Susie's downfall.<br/><br/>A good portion of the book goes</span>
  <span id="freeText11081240209245427960" style="display:none">"An eye for an eye, a tooth for a tooth" Revenge is not always best served cold as the saying goes. A Tooth for a Tooth by JK Franko is the second in the Talion Series. Featuring Susie and Roy who have both lost a loved one and go out to commit the perfect murder. Or was it. They find that they become would-be victims in this novel that is very complex in it's writing. Lots of different characters tell the stories of loss and what could be Roy and Susie's downfall.<br /><br />A good portion of the book goes over events of an Eye for an Eye that sets up the story that is intriguing. There are new characters introduced, even though there are a lot of characters, it helps set the stage for what is to come. You need to understand all the different stories to understand why Roy and Susie Cruise do what they did. But can you really get away with murder? There are also a lot of unexpected twists that surprised me as I was not expecting the story to turn in the direction it did.<br /><br />Like I said, lots of different characters, short chapters. I read in another review that you had to start the series with book 1 to make sense of the story. I did not have that problem though. I am sure that there is some things to be missed if you don't start from the beginning. I intend to go and find the first book and keep an eye out for the third book.<br /><br />I love a good mystery that holds my interest, this book certainly does that. "Don't waste time on revenge, those who hurt you will eventually face their own karma" Pretty much describes this book. I really enjoyed it and recommend it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11081240209245427960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3428776214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3428776214" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15130350-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381949045p2/15130350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3428776214?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/15130350-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15130350-felicia?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15130350-felicia?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15130350-felicia?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3428776214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7574289419850243483">“Well, I wasn’t expecting that,” was my reaction several times through much of the four hundred pages of <i>Tooth for Tooth</i>.<br/><br/>There’s no such thing as a perfect murder, and the karmic consequences of actions kick in doors like an L.A. SWAT team. What began in book 1 as vigilante justice/retribution has flipped to survival of the fittest—or craftiest, in this case—as two of the four bad actors don’t make it to the end of book 2.<br/><br/>The author’s slow, meticulous build continues with details that seem unimp</span>
  <span id="freeText7574289419850243483" style="display:none">“Well, I wasn’t expecting that,” was my reaction several times through much of the four hundred pages of <i>Tooth for Tooth</i>.<br /><br />There’s no such thing as a perfect murder, and the karmic consequences of actions kick in doors like an L.A. SWAT team. What began in book 1 as vigilante justice/retribution has flipped to survival of the fittest—or craftiest, in this case—as two of the four bad actors don’t make it to the end of book 2.<br /><br />The author’s slow, meticulous build continues with details that seem unimportant… until ten pages later when I sat up and my mouth dropped open! Franko also does an impressive job of baiting with distractions then dropping plot twists that change everything.<br /><br />As the rape victim in book 1 who had to watch her rapist go free, Kristy Wise was one of only two characters I had any sympathy for, but after so much death and loss, she showed she was a force to be reckoned with. The other character was Billy Applegate, whose childhood trauma had directed most of his adult life.<br /><br />But everyone else? Nope! I understood them as parents, but they were all just too “into it,” especially Roy with his list of rules, and Deb’s apparent ability to simply forget and move on to the next thing. Tom is pitiful but learning just how dirty his hands are said a lot about him.<br /><br />The cops are also unimpressive. To be fair, law enforcement has endless cases to deal with and don’t have the luxury of focusing on one case, especially one four years old with very little evidence. Yet, college senior Kristy and grieving mom Liz Bareto pieced together most of the puzzle and even shared info with detectives that reinvigorated the case. Not a good look for professional lawmen and investigators.<br /><br />A great continuation of the <i>Talion Series</i> that closes the walls in on the good and bad <i>and</i> the living and dead. Even our anonymous storyteller will not escape unscathed from this tightly woven web of lies and deceit. <i>Tooth for Tooth</i> is complicated, suspenseful, and intelligent, and I highly recommend it… but not without reading book 1, <i>Eye for Eye</i>, first. Motivations and repercussions will not make sense without ALL the details. Fortunately, you have a couple of months to catch up before book 3, <i>Life for Life</i> drops!<br /><br />Enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7574289419850243483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jenn Z at That&#39;s What She&#39;s Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1469742-jenn-z-at-that-s-what-she-s-reading"><img alt="Jenn Z at That&#39;s What She&#39;s Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597107378p2/1469742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3423749216?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn Z at That&#39;s What She&#39;s Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn Z at That&#39;s What She&#39;s Reading" href="/user/show/1469742-jenn-z-at-that-s-what-she-s-reading">Jenn Z at That&#39;s What She&#39;s Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3423749216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12598517291753352862"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594759036i/29814811._SY540_.jpg' width='350' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Last year, I had the opportunity to read and review the first book in this series, EYE FOR EYE, and was absolutely blown away by it. I've been waiting and waiting to get my hands on this installment, and it did not disappoint! Once again, this book is smart, perceptive, gritty, fast paced, and incredibly hard to put down. And, I need the next book NOW!<br/><br/>Picking up immediately where the story left off from the first book, this is no sophomore slump! Fair warning though...this is not one of those se</span>
  <span id="freeText12598517291753352862" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594759036i/29814811._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Last year, I had the opportunity to read and review the first book in this series, EYE FOR EYE, and was absolutely blown away by it. I've been waiting and waiting to get my hands on this installment, and it did not disappoint! Once again, this book is smart, perceptive, gritty, fast paced, and incredibly hard to put down. And, I need the next book NOW!<br><br>Picking up immediately where the story left off from the first book, this is no sophomore slump! Fair warning though...this is not one of those series that you can just start from anywhere. The story is so well conceptualized and executed, unfolding through multiple perspectives and plot lines that you'll definitely need to start with EYE FOR EYE. <br><br><b>"Revenge, like seduction, is a process. It is a game of inches."</b><br><br>The Law of Talion or the principle that a person who has injured another person is to be penalized to a similar degree by the injured party remains at the forefront of each character's motivation and drive in dealing with the tragedies inflicted upon them. But this time around, Machiavellian vengeance begins to weave its way into solving each dilemma; however, getting ahead doesn't always mean you'll make it to the finish line. This is certainly a fascinating exploration into the role of the highly unlikeable character or characters, and the author has an understanding of human nature that makes the rawness of these characters come alive. You may not like them or their deeds, but you can completely understand where they are coming from that's for sure!<br><br>The many twists and turns throughout are masterfully done, making it difficult to trust anyone or predict where the story is going to go. And combined with the fast-paced chapters, the tension and suspense kept mounting until the very end. The author's writing style is engaging and seamlessly connects the idea of retribution throughout, forcing readers to constantly consider exactly what we would do if circumstances were placed directly into our own lives as well. This was an intense thriller told from various points of view that added incredible layering to the growing suspense, while also building anticipation for the final showdown, but things are far from over and no one should get too comfortable.<br><br>This second course is dark, dangerous, and deliciously deceptive, and I can't wait for more!<br><br><i>Many thanks to the author and Partners in Crime Virtual Book Blog Tours for providing me a free copy of the book. This is my honest and thoughtful review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12598517291753352862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3266651676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7510578014926089823">Tooth for Tooth is a fantastic follow-up to Eye for Eye, bringing back the intoxicating voice and intrigue of the first book in the Talion series.<br/><br/>This is one of those books that builds piece-by-piece, so it's almost difficult to review without offering spoilers, but what I love about this book (beyond the writing and intrigue!) is that it takes an unusual vantage in the way it tackles a suspense series. There are so many great series out there that follow a detective or agent of some sort, makin</span>
  <span id="freeText7510578014926089823" style="display:none">Tooth for Tooth is a fantastic follow-up to Eye for Eye, bringing back the intoxicating voice and intrigue of the first book in the Talion series.<br /><br />This is one of those books that builds piece-by-piece, so it's almost difficult to review without offering spoilers, but what I love about this book (beyond the writing and intrigue!) is that it takes an unusual vantage in the way it tackles a suspense series. There are so many great series out there that follow a detective or agent of some sort, making them the center-piece, but this series works to encompass a whole cast of characters and crimes while remaining true to the genre and to the details that made the first book in the series so powerful. In doing that, it accomplishes a great deal, and it's no small thing to say that the book still manages to be full of twists, surprises, and moments of intrigue that will only engage a reader all the more.<br /><br />This is a powerful piece of story-telling, and with Franko's attention to suspense, psychology, and criminal behavior, it's also impossible to put down. The one caveat? Make sure you read the first book first if you want to get the most out of this one!</span>

<div id="review_3320087520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3320087520" />
    <a title="Alyson Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66660579-alyson-read"><img alt="Alyson Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491494945p2/66660579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3320087520?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyson Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyson Read" href="/user/show/66660579-alyson-read">Alyson Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/52418560-tooth-for-tooth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3320087520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5097080523016465287">The law of talion - lex talionis - requires punishment of an injury by inflicting a similar injury on the offender, an injury similar in kind and degree. An eye for an eye, a fracture for a fracture, a tooth for a tooth. Old Testament justice, but just how literally would most people take it to mean? The book begins with a prologue that dates back many years to the abuse of a child. Just how this fits into the story becomes apparent much later on. We first met Roy and Susie Cruise in book 1, Eye</span>
  <span id="freeText5097080523016465287" style="display:none">The law of talion - lex talionis - requires punishment of an injury by inflicting a similar injury on the offender, an injury similar in kind and degree. An eye for an eye, a fracture for a fracture, a tooth for a tooth. Old Testament justice, but just how literally would most people take it to mean? The book begins with a prologue that dates back many years to the abuse of a child. Just how this fits into the story becomes apparent much later on. We first met Roy and Susie Cruise in book 1, Eye For Eye, and it really is essential to read this book first since so much happens in it and book 2 follows directly on. Although the past events are referred to during the first half of the book, the reader really needs to know the detail to fully appreciate how all the main characters have come to where they are by September 2019. There are also many sub plots bubbling away in tandem to the main story of the murder of rapist Joe Harlan Jnr as other characters try to discover their own truths and exact their own revenge. <br />It is extremely hard to give a full review without giving away too many spoilers to those who have yet to read the first book but here goes! Susie has now been involved in three deaths, directly or indirectly. Roy has been involved in four. Death does seem to follow them around but they are perfectionists and believe they are untouchable. The bond between them is very strong but will never be as strong as the bond between Susie and Deb, and Roy knows more about that bond than he lets on to his wife. Roy needs to confront Susie about what happened to Joan and Susie needs to confront Roy about what happened to Deb. Roy has got away with the perfect murder once and now he's planning another one. And this time the revenge is to be taken in another country. All the main characters are beginning to come together and are employing help to find out what has really happened as they start to air their own suspicions. We meet again Detective Eddie Garza, Liz Bareto, Tom, Deb and Kristy Wise, David Kim and Senator Joe Harlan Snr, together with some interesting new people, one with very unsavoury inclinations. They are all getting closer to the truth but nearly everyone is holding something back and keeping secrets. Once again the narrator knows and sees all, although now he knows how much danger he could face if he ever told the truth. It's a complicated and tangled plot where the truth gradually surfaces in different places and to different people, with shocking and devastating consequences for those involved. And with the truth comes the fact that the tables start to turn and the hunters find themselves being hunted as everything they knew starts to fall apart and those singing bones start to surface. Just as some things start to make sense, others are left on a knife edge as the story promises to continue in book 3, Life For Life, which I am eagerly awaiting!! 5*</span>
  <a data-text-id="5097080523016465287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3267944895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13811057216391195133"><strong>Fangs!</strong><br/><br/>Two of the best books I have ever read! I am so looking forward to the third in the fall! They left me breathless!</span>

<div id="review_3249182769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3249182769" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24574769-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575849041p2/24574769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3249182769?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/24574769-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3249182769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9737048161787830395">Another page-turning read from J.K. Franko! I read the first book (Eye for Eye) when it came out and absolutely loved it--it's a rare joy to find an author who has mastered both the art of writing suspense and also how to interweave some of the pressing issues of our time. <br/><br/>The writing style has plenty of details to immerse you in the world the author builds and to keep you invested in the characters without going overboard and becoming tedious. There are a ton of fun smaller details (some of whi</span>
  <span id="freeText9737048161787830395" style="display:none">Another page-turning read from J.K. Franko! I read the first book (Eye for Eye) when it came out and absolutely loved it--it's a rare joy to find an author who has mastered both the art of writing suspense and also how to interweave some of the pressing issues of our time. <br /><br />The writing style has plenty of details to immerse you in the world the author builds and to keep you invested in the characters without going overboard and becoming tedious. There are a ton of fun smaller details (some of which caused me to react out loud when I read them...my dog thought I was crazy for randomly shouting "NOOOO!!!"), and this is a great book if you're like me and enjoy trying to pick out the minutiae that foreshadow plot twists later on. I was definitely satisfied at the end (although I'm now eagerly waiting for the next book in the series). There were some excellent plot twists that I didn't see coming in spite of my best efforts to figure things out ahead of time, and there's a ton of potential plot lines for the next book.<br /><br />I'd recommend this to anyone who likes thrillers, suspense, and procedurals. Tooth for Tooth is an awesome blend of some of the best parts of those genres, and it's just as fun to re-read to look for the hints the author plants along the way about how things turn out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9737048161787830395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8685033642321418861" style="display:none">Readers really should read book one first. This is my fault as I did not read book one first. I thought I could just jump into this series. Sometimes you can and other times, the series is meant to be read in chronological order as is the case of this book.<br /><br />I say that because this book felt very character driven. Therefore, because I had not read the prior novel, I did not have all of the background history between all of the characters. In addition, there was not as strong a connection towards them or the motive for the killings. <br /><br />Honestly, I did think that this book would be a bit more graphic in the violence but it was not. It was mainly focused on the characters. Overall, I did like this book but my opinions may have been strong for it if I had read the prior book. </span>

<div id="review_3447180456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3447180456" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4239132-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312333230p2/4239132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3447180456?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/4239132-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/52418560-tooth-for-tooth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3447180456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6774641586515666228">In Tooth For Tooth, book two in the Talion Series, author J.K. Franko takes the reader behind the scenes of a riveting crime thriller as the characters continue on the slippery slope of pursuing the Law of Talion, seeking revenge for tragedies that have occurred to their families.<br/><br/>In this installment of the series, Author J.K. Franko asks the reader the following questions: what would you do if you got away with murder? How much farther would you go to get revenge? Can you stop, or is the thirst </span>
  <span id="freeText6774641586515666228" style="display:none">In Tooth For Tooth, book two in the Talion Series, author J.K. Franko takes the reader behind the scenes of a riveting crime thriller as the characters continue on the slippery slope of pursuing the Law of Talion, seeking revenge for tragedies that have occurred to their families.<br /><br />In this installment of the series, Author J.K. Franko asks the reader the following questions: what would you do if you got away with murder? How much farther would you go to get revenge? Can you stop, or is the thirst for revenge too enticing? And what do you do to make sure that the loose ends aka "singing bones" don't come back to bite you?<br /><br />Tooth For Tooth is a riveting story that easily draws the reader in from the start. I would recommend that you read the first book, Eye For Eye, as Tooth For Tooth continues the storyline, even though the author does recap scenes from the first book throughout the second book. The readers will be captivated as the author weaves a thoroughly intriguing and complicated story that follows married couple Susie Font and Roy Cruise, as they take the law into their own hands with calculated choices and precision, and an eye to limiting the consequences and getting caught.<br /><br />The author provides the reader with a fascinating and richly detailed crime thriller set in Miami and Austin. You can't help but get drawn into this complicated, fascinating, and multi-layered story told in an alternating first and third person narrative by Susie and Roy's therapist. Susie and Roy play an intricate cat-n-mouse game, but there are others that have them in their crosshairs as they search for connections into the rash of deaths by the devious couple, oh what a tangled web they weave!<br /><br />Tooth For Tooth has enough drama, secrets, deception, and tension that keeps the reader on their toes and guessing as they turn the pages, wondering where the madness would end. But alas ... the author teases the reader with another surprising cliffhanger ending that will leave them wanting more as they await the continuation of the story in Life For Life, book three in the series.<br /><br />Tooth For Tooth is a gripping and chilling crime thriller that is a must read for all crime thriller fans.<br /><br />Disclaimer: I borrowed a copy of the book from my Kindle Unlimited program. I am also participating in a virtual book tour vent hosted by Partners In Crime Virtual Book Tours.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jerseygirlbookreviews.blogspot.com/2020/07/tooth-for-tooth-by-jk-franko-vbt-book.html">https://jerseygirlbookreviews.blogspo...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6774641586515666228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12819198061796443217">Phew, this trilogy...<br/><br/>I have to say right off the bat, I absolutely despised almost every single character in this series. There was just one I liked and respected.However, I also found them all incredibly intriguing! It was like watching a suspenseful day-time soap; I just couldn't wait to see what was going to happen next.<br/><br/>My only slight complaint, and it's my common complaint, was that a lot of this seemed very repetitive to me.   <span id="freeText12819198061796443217" style="display:none">Phew, this trilogy...<br /><br />I have to say right off the bat, I absolutely despised almost every single character in this series. There was just one I liked and respected.However, I also found them all incredibly intriguing! It was like watching a suspenseful day-time soap; I just couldn't wait to see what was going to happen next.<br /><br />My only slight complaint, and it's my common complaint, was that a lot of this seemed very repetitive to me. Unfortunately, that may just be because I read the three back to back, I'm not totally sure. Where there are so many characters and moving pieces, this could help remind readers of certain things, but for me it really bogged the stories down.<br /><br /><b>Book Two: Tooth For Tooth</b><br /><br />In book two, I really enjoyed getting to know more characters that were tangled up in this crazy web!<br /><br />Just like the first book, revenge is planned, murder occurs, but the story also gets even more complicated! Roy and Susie are certainly more confident in this one than they were in book one.<br /><br />I enjoyed the mystery element of this book as we watched Kristy on her quest to find out what was going on as well as how a new player in this twisted puzzle was going to fit in...<br /><br />The same case here with the epilogue. It tied up a few loose ends wonderfully but also made me want to shout, what's next?!<br /><br />This was my favorite passage from this book:<br />The funny thing about nostalgia is, we only tend to remember the good things about the good ol’ days. It’s only when we stop, and actually walk back into that old high school building, that all the bad shit comes rushing back.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer188888430780952405">I found Tooth for Tooth fascinating, mesmerizing, and gritty. Murder isn’t appealing, but JK Franko takes you inside the minds of a couple that finds killing rewarding as they organize the demise perfectly. This novel is written by Roy and Susie’s psychologist, prepared as a backup encase something should happen to her, a memoir of their office visits. As Roy and Susie prepare to go out of the country, a detective in Texas and one in Florida compare notes. Can they find the missing piece that ti</span>
  <span id="freeText188888430780952405" style="display:none">I found Tooth for Tooth fascinating, mesmerizing, and gritty. Murder isn’t appealing, but JK Franko takes you inside the minds of a couple that finds killing rewarding as they organize the demise perfectly. This novel is written by Roy and Susie’s psychologist, prepared as a backup encase something should happen to her, a memoir of their office visits. As Roy and Susie prepare to go out of the country, a detective in Texas and one in Florida compare notes. Can they find the missing piece that ties it all together?  <br />   <br />Tooth for Tooth by JK Franko continues the Talion series, this being the second book. We begin with a note from the source of this journal and why she must recount her relationship to Roy and Susie. The author spins a complex web of intricate relationships, revenge, and justice. Judgment and destruction comes, but the arbitrator isn’t always the first, or second, choice avenger. Overall, I am enthralled by this author. I look forward to the next book; Life for Life.     </span>

      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TB2ixOhsNX86uPjckju73RoHZw4UTKTSSHUnglOEvwan01zJMX2QbHpH+jtq8ishqCqjKMmZZC1PHH7ddWzATQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rchqLSZ1tpPnBhcn2uN4iLXnIGyTRnSQuWTWfoXz8FpGBpQg/2QTgKf5FcAiKuh0B8rkSk6TtG++DY8hoxuPEQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/18789144.J_K_Franko"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1548784205p3/18789144.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/18789144.J_K_Franko">J.K. Franko

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8301850249846203041">I grew up in Texas in the seventies, and although I really wanted to go into writing and film from an early age, my parents (Cuban-American) were NOT on board.<br/><br/>They believed there were only three acceptable career paths for a male child: doctor, lawyer, and architect. <br/><br/>After a disastrous first year of college pre-Med (too much fun, not enough study), I ended up getting a BA in philosophy (not accept</span>
  <span id="freeText8301850249846203041" style="display:none">I grew up in Texas in the seventies, and although I really wanted to go into writing and film from an early age, my parents (Cuban-American) were NOT on board.<br /><br />They believed there were only three acceptable career paths for a male child: doctor, lawyer, and architect. <br /><br />After a disastrous first year of college pre-Med (too much fun, not enough study), I ended up getting a BA in philosophy (not acceptable), then I went to law school (salvaging the family name).<br /><br />In law school, I was lucky enough to be selected for law journal and my articles have been cited by courts and recognized on the National Law Journal’s “Worth Reading” list – which for law is like a top review in the New York Times (pretty cool).<br /><br />After ten years as a trial lawyer, I decided that law and family life weren’t compatible. So, I went back to school for an MBA, and later pursued a PhD, crossing the line from well-educated to over-educated around the turn of the century.<br /><br />With these credentials, I was able to leave law for corporate America, where I got to spend long stints working in Europe and Asia.<br /><br />It was my wife who pushed me to write novels. And, after thousands of hours writing, and seven or eight literary miscarriages over the course of eighteen years, I am now a published fiction author!<br /><br />We live all in South Florida (for now) with our six (yes - 6) dogs and one cat.<br /><br />I love boating, running, and chocolate.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8301850249846203041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
